The SMILES string CCCOC(C)C represents a molecule with the following structure:
- "CCC" indicates a propyl chain (three carbons: CH3-CH2-CH2-).
- "O" indicates an oxygen atom, suggesting an ether linkage.
- "C(C)C" indicates a carbon atom connected to two methyl groups, which likely represents an isopropyl-like fragment (CH(CH3)-CH3), but in the context of the preceding "O", it suggests the oxygen is bonded to a carbon that has a methyl branch.
- Parsing it fully: CCC-O-C(C)C means a propyl group (CCC) connected via oxygen (O) to a carbon that has two additional carbons, likely CH(CH3)CH3, but more accurately, it is CH(CH3)2 if we consider standard SMILES interpretation of branching. However, looking at the exact string, C(C)C after O suggests O-CH(CH3)-CH3, i.e., a secondary carbon with one methyl and one ethyl-like continuation, but in standard SMILES, CCCOC(C)C is interpreted as CH3-CH2-CH2-O-CH(CH3)-CH3, a propyl ether with a 2-propyl group.

So, the molecule is CH3-CH2-CH2-O-CH(CH3)-CH3, an ether with a propyl group and a 2-propyl (isopropyl-like) group, totaling 6 carbons and one oxygen.

- **Functional Group**: Ether (R-O-R'), which suggests moderate polarity.
- **Carbon Chain Length**: Six carbons total, with branching (one methyl branch on the carbon adjacent to oxygen on one side).
